<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer15541045243513044014">In a suspense novel of astounding power and depth, Jodi Compton unleashes a haunting tale of secrets and betrayal...and of one woman's search for her missing husband that spirals into a dark journey strewn with bitter truths and damged lives. Here debut novelist Compton introduces an extraordinary character: Detective Sarah Pribek, a woman of strength, complexity, and inst</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15541045243513044014">In a suspense novel of astounding power and depth, Jodi Compton unleashes a haunting tale of secrets and betrayal...and of one woman's search for her missing husband that spirals into a dark journey strewn with bitter truths and damged lives. Here debut novelist Compton introduces an extraordinary character: Detective Sarah Pribek, a woman of strength, complexity, and instinct, a woman caught in an unimaginable nightmare...<br /><br /><strong>The 37th Hour</strong><br /><br />On a chilly Minnesota morning, Sarah comes home to the house she shares with her husband and fellow cop, Michael Shiloh. Shiloh was supposed to be in Virginia, starting his training with the FBI. A seasoned missing-persons investigator, Sarah is used to anxious calls from wives and parents. She's used to the innocent explanations that resolve so many of her cases. But from the moment she learns that he never arrived at Quantico, she feels a terrible foreboding. Now, beneath the bed in which they make love, Sarah finds Shiloh's neatly packed bag. And in that instant the cop in her knows: Her husband has disappeared.<br /><br />Suddenly Sarah finds herself at the beginning of the kind of investigation she has made so often. The kind that she and her ex-partner, Genevieve, solved routinely -- until a brutal crime stole Genevieve's daughter and ended her career. The kind that pries open family secrets and hidden lives. For Sarah this investigation will mean going back to the beginning, to Shiloh's religion-steeped childhood in Utah, the rift that separated him from his family -- and the one horrifying case that struck them both too close to home. As Sarah turns over more and more unknown ground in her husband's past, she sees her lover and friend change into a stranger before her eyes. And as she moves further down a trail of shocking surprises and bitter revelations, Sarah is about to discover that her worst fear -- that Shiloh is dead -- may be less painful than what she will learn next...<br /><br />In a novel of runaway tension, Jodi Compton masterfully weaves together the quiet details of everyday life with the moments that can shatter them forever. At once a beguiling mystery and a powerful rumination on family, friendship, and loss, <strong>The 37th Hour</strong> is a thriller that will catch you off guard at every turn -- instantly compelling and utterly impossible to put down.<br /><br /><br /><em>From the Hardcover edition.</em></span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]&gt;
</script>  <script type="text/javascript">
  //&lt;![CDATA[
      var $ratingGraph = $j('#rating_graph');
      var $copy;
      if ($ratingGraph.length &gt; 0) {
          $copy = $ratingGraph.clone();
          $j('#rating_details_tip_graph').remove();
          $copy.attr('id', 'rating_details_tip_graph');
          $copy.find('script').remove();
          $j('#rating_details_tip').prepend($copy);
      }
  //]]&gt;
  </script>
</div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer196140997">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15741540839127047224">You think by the title of this book that its all the meat of it will take place in an hour.. the 37th hour. It was all in the time period of 6 days. Almost leisurely investigating which in this case wouldnt be plausable seeing as how it is her husband who is missing. I did like a lot of the way she wrote things and the words she used to describe things.. and they say that when tramatic things are happening in your life things that happened not too long ago seem like a century ago.. well Compton</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15741540839127047224">You think by the title of this book that its all the meat of it will take place in an hour.. the 37th hour. It was all in the time period of 6 days. Almost leisurely investigating which in this case wouldnt be plausable seeing as how it is her husband who is missing. I did like a lot of the way she wrote things and the words she used to describe things.. and they say that when tramatic things are happening in your life things that happened not too long ago seem like a century ago.. well Compton did a wonderful job at writing that feeling.. the beginning of the book almost seemed like it wasnt part if the book, like it was a prequel. this book was an easy read and not as dark as you expect it to be.. i did not feel that anxious feeling i get when i read other missing persons books. that feeling where things need to be done quicker before something happens to them. i didnt get that suspense. Over all this book was less of a mystery or missing person book than it was just about how she met this guy and his and her life up until then. it was more of a quest to learn more about this man who was a independant type than it was a quest to find where he is. I was disappointed. But it wasnt without entertainment. i liked reading it, its just not the kind of book it says it is.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11678279410418870305">Recently promoted Detective Sara Pribeck is also a new wife. While she’s known her husband Shiloh for five years, what she doesn’t know about him probably exceeds what she does. Their marriage is only two months old when he disappears, after having encouraged her to make an overnight visit to her traumatized partner, Gen.<br /><br />Naturally, Sara sets out to find her husband, and she hasn’t many clues to follow. Bit by bit, it becomes evident that the murder of partner Gen’s teenaged daughter, which happe</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11678279410418870305">Recently promoted Detective Sara Pribeck is also a new wife. While she’s known her husband Shiloh for five years, what she doesn’t know about him probably exceeds what she does. Their marriage is only two months old when he disappears, after having encouraged her to make an overnight visit to her traumatized partner, Gen.<br /><br />Naturally, Sara sets out to find her husband, and she hasn’t many clues to follow. Bit by bit, it becomes evident that the murder of partner Gen’s teenaged daughter, which happened in the recent past, is somehow connected to what happened to Shiloh.<br /><br />The 37th Hour gets off to a strong, promising start, but fails to fulfill that promise with a slow middle and a weak, rather rushed conclusion. Threads raising questions about relationships, morals, revenge, and forgiveness wind up muddled and unresolved, and the book’s final chapter leaves the reader hanging. A sequel seems likely, but author Compton would do well to strengthen her plotting skills before publishing again.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1236781623">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9017758057544203318">I enjoyed this story as a novel. It didn't matter to me that it wasn't very exciting and suspenseful. More of a mystery rather than a cop thriller kind of story. I was reading it on an exercise bike and it was perfect for that because it was slow reading and jumps around to flash backs a lot. That is so clich</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9017758057544203318">I enjoyed this story as a novel. It didn't matter to me that it wasn't very exciting and suspenseful. More of a mystery rather than a cop thriller kind of story. I was reading it on an exercise bike and it was perfect for that because it was slow reading and jumps around to flash backs a lot. She gives good clues so the reader can guess at what the mystery might be before the protagonist does. It was too bad that so many characters had reddish hair and were extremely attractive. That is so cliche in mysteries. <br /><br />What I especially like was that the sex is behind closed doors and they are actually married. You don't have to read about erections etc. The other thing that was a nice change was that the author had a great vocabulary and I kept wishing I had a dictionary with me. There wasn't the F word and terms like Bastard sprinkled all over. <br /><br />It was also a good change to have a deaf person in the story. You could see how isolated and unloved she felt because her family didn't make an effort to learn sign language. I was confused about who the father of her daughter was or if she was actually ever married.<br /><br />I liked the fact that many of the characters are women even though the person missing was a man. Why the police force or the FBI wasn't out looking for the cop that disappeared was hard to understand. The wife is the only one that seems to care and has to look for him unofficially. He could easily have been nabbed by someone he put behind bars that is out of prison. The ending wasn't all that satisfying because there are several ethical issues that I found disturbing. The big question is: do the ends justify the means? I like it when a cop does 'the right thing'. The book really makes you think about what is the right thing under certain circumstances. Despite this I still want to read the sequel and find out what happens next. Does someone get away with murder? Do I want them to?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9017758057544203318">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Without revealing to much, good people seem to do some crazy things at the end which seem completely out of their character.<br /><br /><br />Another thing I noticed though is that all characters, wherever possible, are women -- from the main character, her partner and best friend, her husband's sisters... up to the taxi driver. <br /><br />Male characters play a secondary role and are usually either baffled at what is happening (the new partner), oblivious to obvious facts (the husband's brothers), strange (the husband) or simply evil (the main bad guy).<br /><br />There are much better detective stories out there, IMHO.<br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13424856584938742275">Jodi Compton's The 37th Hour is a great debut novel with a hanging ending that leaves you with a great deal to ponder. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[<br />How could it come to such a point where two cops, good at what they do, fine upstanding citizens both end up as suspects in murders?   <span style="display:none" id="freeText13424856584938742275">Jodi Compton's The 37th Hour is a great debut novel with a hanging ending that leaves you with a great deal to ponder. <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[<br />How could it come to such a point where two cops, good at what they do, fine upstanding citizens both end up as suspects in murders? How could the criminal justice system let murders and rapists off on technicalities? How could a man mislead his wife so he could go and finish what the courts let get away? Sarah Pribeck and Mike Shiloh have only been married two months when he disappears. He should have been on the way to the FBI for 4 months of training in preparations for a career in the FBI. Instead it turns out he goes to run down the murderer and rapist who killed the daughter of a close friend. Sarah's search for Mike takes her to Utah and revelations about Mike's relationship with his sister that shock her and may end their marriage. To make things worse, the murdered girl's mother, Genevieve, is Sarah's former partner and in the heat of passion Genevieve kills Shorty -- the man Shiloh couldn't bring himself to run down. As the book ends, Genevieve is on the way to Paris, Mike is in jail for multiple felony charges, his career ruined and Sarah is a prime suspect in the murder of Shorty. The first 36 hours in a missing persons case are supposed to be the best window of opportunity to find someone-- what happens in the 37th hour after Mike disappears and Sarah sets out to find him is quick a shock. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18137601202118345896">A reasonably well-done "where'd they go?" mystery, especially for a first-time author. I like that it was not a straight through telling of events. Well constructed flashbacks and side trips were helpful. Knots were tied, or untied, without straining the chords, a feat in itself.<br /><br />Detective Sarah Pribek's husband of 2 months has gone missing, leaving no discernible trace. In her search we travel from Minnesota to Utah to New Mexico and back trying to learn elements of his background of which she w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18137601202118345896">A reasonably well-done "where'd they go?" mystery, especially for a first-time author. I like that it was not a straight through telling of events. Well constructed flashbacks and side trips were helpful. Knots were tied, or untied, without straining the chords, a feat in itself.<br /><br />Detective Sarah Pribek's husband of 2 months has gone missing, leaving no discernible trace. In her search we travel from Minnesota to Utah to New Mexico and back trying to learn elements of his background of which she was wholly ignorant. It is no help that Shiloh was not one to talk about anything but the current time and the future. <br /><br />As Sarah uncovers details in his background with his family in Utah, she learns a different story than that which he tells.<br /><br />I loved that my expectations of "the story will now go this way" and it would abruptly jag off in a different direction. And, yet, each jag leaves a piece of information for the reader to hold as the puzzle of what happened is slowly pieced together. Working toward the biggest mystery of all. Is Shiloh alive or did he die somewhere along his own mysterious path.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18137601202118345896">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_121954223">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/121954223" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3749347-kae-cheatham" class="left imgcol" title="Kae Cheatham"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442472981p2/3749347.jpg" alt="Kae Cheatham" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/121954223?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 16, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3749347-kae-cheatham" class="user" title="Kae Cheatham">Kae Cheatham</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3749347-kae-cheatham?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer121954223">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9032792016512093488">Sarah Pribek is a detective for a Minnesota County Sheriffs' department. She investigates missing persons. But her job really hits home when she must investigate the disappearance of her husband of two months, Mike Shiloh. Mike was supposed to be in Quantico, training for the FBI, but he never arrived. As she delves into the mystery, back stories are told, particularly about her partner Genevieve who's teenage daughter was brutally raped and murdered, and the perp went free. Sarah and Mike had b</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9032792016512093488">Sarah Pribek is a detective for a Minnesota County Sheriffs' department. She investigates missing persons. But her job really hits home when she must investigate the disappearance of her husband of two months, Mike Shiloh. Mike was supposed to be in Quantico, training for the FBI, but he never arrived. As she delves into the mystery, back stories are told, particularly about her partner Genevieve who's teenage daughter was brutally raped and murdered, and the perp went free. Sarah and Mike had been with Gen when the battered daughter was found. <br />Another back story is about Mike and what makes up his stoic, inscrutable character. Another gives hints at Sarah's background; still another tells how the romantic involvement between Sarah and Mike developed.<br /><br />All the stories are woven through Sarah's search for clues about what happened to Mike, including her trip to Utah to interview members of his estranged family.<br /><br />In the end, the stories meld to a probable resolution with a twist that hints at future Sarah Pribek mysteries.<br />Told in first person, the writing is smooth. I never felt a gripping "need to know" regarding Mike, who I didn't particularly care for (and liked even less at the end of the book). The book's ending provides a chilling depiction of human grief and character. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9032792016512093488">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer168833822">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6399340269244191284">MAY CONTAIN SPOILERS.<br /><br />The characters were believable, and likeable.<br /><br />Starts out as a case of a missing husband (who's a competent cop.)<br /><br />The ending bummed me out -- not only does the woman cop who's central seem like she's going to get indicted/convicted/sentenced.<br /><br />But the final events leading to that outcome were plain crazy.<br /><br />Why would her cop husband, who is good enough to get accepted to the FBI academy, just go off the deep end and kill the guy who killed the wife's cop partner's daughter. (partner</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6399340269244191284">MAY CONTAIN SPOILERS.<br /><br />The characters were believable, and likeable.<br /><br />Starts out as a case of a missing husband (who's a competent cop.)<br /><br />The ending bummed me out -- not only does the woman cop who's central seem like she's going to get indicted/convicted/sentenced.<br /><br />But the final events leading to that outcome were plain crazy.<br /><br />Why would her cop husband, who is good enough to get accepted to the FBI academy, just go off the deep end and kill the guy who killed the wife's cop partner's daughter. (partner is another woman.) This ruins his own career, guarantees he and his wife can't be together.<br /><br />Also turns out the husband committed incest w. a sister - in their younger days, and then just a few years back -- all unknown to the wife, until she starts hunting for the husband, and unravels his mysterious past.<br /><br />Then the wife cop goes out w. her cop partner (who's on extended bereavement leave after daughter's rape/murder) and ends up being accessory to the perp's murder. Partner goes free (skips to Europe) while wife cop knows, at end, she's going down.<br /><br />Again, I liked the characters. But I don't think the author did -- or she wouldn't have wasted them on such an implausible story.<br /><br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_161849999">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/161849999" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5176688-phoebe" class="left imgcol" title="Phoebe"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1395949425p2/5176688.jpg" alt="Phoebe" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/161849999?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 18, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5176688-phoebe" class="user" title="Phoebe">Phoebe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/739147.The_37th_Hour" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440241362" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5176688-phoebe?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer161849999">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3643933468026963859">Sarah Pribek specializes in missing person cases, which theoretically should come in handy when she realizes her husband has disappeared somewhere between home and Quantico, where he was meant to begin training for the FBI. It's only as she begins searching for him that she realizes just how little she has to go on. Mike Shiloh is a private man, they've only been married for two months, and she knows very little about his past that could offer up any clues.<br /><br />While this book had a lot of potential</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3643933468026963859">Sarah Pribek specializes in missing person cases, which theoretically should come in handy when she realizes her husband has disappeared somewhere between home and Quantico, where he was meant to begin training for the FBI. It's only as she begins searching for him that she realizes just how little she has to go on. Mike Shiloh is a private man, they've only been married for two months, and she knows very little about his past that could offer up any clues.<br /><br />While this book had a lot of potential and a few interesting characters, I felt the author spent too much time detailing out past events. I found myself skimming over entire italicized sections of 'memory' just to get back to the main plot, while recognizing that somehow everything I was being told would end up related or important. That in and of itself was something of a disappointment, because it took away some of the dimension of the book. Also, while I recognize that neither Pribek nor her husband were 'sentimental' types, I sometimes felt like her husband almost wasn't worth looking for considering how flat and emotionless he seemed.<br /><br />And, finally, as many have said before, the ending wasn't all that great. For me, it wasn't the resolution so much as the details about Shiloh's past that feel heavy-handed and unnecessary. They do not effect the main story, but somehow manage to cast a shadow over the writing for being so over the top.<br /><br />This book is a fun read if you're just looking for something to pass the time, but there are other mystery books I would recommend before it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3643933468026963859">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7133782-cathy?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7133782-cathy?shelf=series" class="actionLinkLite">series</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer512406794">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3412381251775692160">From the Goodreads book summary: "In a suspense novel of astounding power and depth, Jodi Compton unleashes a haunting tale of secrets and betrayal... and of one woman's search for her missing husband that spirals into a dark journey strewn with bitter truths and damaged lives." Wow! And yup, that's what the book was. I really liked the characters - well written, both heroic and flawed at the same time. The story took many twists and turns; I really had no idea how it was going to turn out - and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3412381251775692160">From the Goodreads book summary: "In a suspense novel of astounding power and depth, Jodi Compton unleashes a haunting tale of secrets and betrayal... and of one woman's search for her missing husband that spirals into a dark journey strewn with bitter truths and damaged lives." Wow! And yup, that's what the book was. I really liked the characters - well written, both heroic and flawed at the same time. The story took many twists and turns; I really had no idea how it was going to turn out - and of course, I was wrong with all of my guesses. Detective Sarah Pribek is searching for her missing husband Michael Shiloh (also a cop, who should have been at FBI training in Quantico). As Sarah searches, Ms. Compton skillfully fills us in on the back story of Sarah and Shiloh, connecting with characters from both present and past. Secondary and tertiary story lines were woven in between the main story beautifully - well written and made sense - nothing seemed contrived (to me anyway). Again, the ending is really not what I expected, in several ways. <br /><br />This book, also found at a second-hand store for $1, is a definite keeper - I will remember this story for a long time and will most likely reread it at some point. Excellent! </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_807490098">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/807490098" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/13317542-booksnpics" class="left imgcol" title="BooksnPics"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446195822p2/13317542.jpg" alt="BooksnPics" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/807490098?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 30, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/13317542-booksnpics" class="user" title="BooksnPics">BooksnPics</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/19522521-la-37-me-heure" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer807490098">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7812136711639692865">Avec ce premier roman de Jodi Compton, nous faisons la connaissance de Sarah Pribek, inspecteur à la brigade des personnes disparues. Son mari, Michael Shiloh est inspecteur dans la police de Minneapolis mais s'apprête à partir au centre de formation du FBI à Quantico pour une période de quatre mois. Lorsqu'elle rentre chez elle et découvre la maison vide, elle pense que celui-ci vient de partir pour la Virginie. En découvrant qu'il n'est jamais arrivé à destination, Sarah va mener son enquête.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7812136711639692865">Avec ce premier roman de Jodi Compton, nous faisons la connaissance de Sarah Pribek, inspecteur à la brigade des personnes disparues. Son mari, Michael Shiloh est inspecteur dans la police de Minneapolis mais s'apprête à partir au centre de formation du FBI à Quantico pour une période de quatre mois. Lorsqu'elle rentre chez elle et découvre la maison vide, elle pense que celui-ci vient de partir pour la Virginie. En découvrant qu'il n'est jamais arrivé à destination, Sarah va mener son enquête. Interrogeant les voisins, retraçant son possible parcours, traversant les Etats-Unis, à la recherche de son mari, Sarah va se voir confrontée elle-même à l'angoisse des familles de personnes portées disparues. Allant de découvertes en découvertes sur la personnalité de son mari ainsi que sur son passé, Sarah aura-t-elle le temps de retrouver sa trace? <br />"Geneviève m'avait dit un jour, dans les premiers temps de ma carrière d'inspecteur: "Quand tu te retrouve avec une affaire de disparition, une vraie, une affaire qui t'inspire un mauvais pressentiment, les vingt-quatre ou trente-six premières heures sont capitales. Vas-y à fond. Et vite". La plupart du temps, il s'agissait de disparitions d'enfants. Parfois aussi, c'étaient des femmes qui avaient disparus dans des circonstances inquiétantes: traces d'effraction à leur domicile ou bien plusieurs amis ayant vu un ex-fiancé sinistre rôder dans les parages. Rien de tel concernant la disparition de Shiloh. Dans son cas, les trente-six heures s'étaient écoulées sans que je m'aperçoive qu'il avait disparu." (p.84)<br /><br />"La 37e heure" est un polar rondement mené qui répond à toutes les caractéristiques que l'on en attend: un personnage principal attachant, une disparition mystérieuse, une enquête de longue haleine, et beaucoup d'interrogations. Son écriture est simple mais efficace et elle sait nous tenir en haleine à travers un texte dense nous laissant peu de temps morts. Jodi Compton nous livre ici un polar qui se veut somme toute classique où la psychologie des personnages tient une place primordiale. Un très beau début pour cet auteur, dont je suivrai très certainement l'actualité, même si l'issue du roman nous laisse un peu sur notre faim...laissant présager d'autres romans... Son deuxième opus "Les jeux sont faits" est également disponible en version ebook aux Editions des Deux Terres. <br />Je remercie MyBoox et les Editions des Deux Terres pour cette découverte que je recommande à tous les amateurs de polars.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7812136711639692865">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13413460063573111530">I wasn't sure about sticking with this slow-moving novel, but I did. On one hand I was curious about what had happened in the various plot threads. On the other, I didn't feel any connection or fondness for the characters. My curiosity was idle, not deeply engaged as it would have been if I'd come to care for any of the characters. </span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8654120546288661878">This was my bus read this week and it was a good one, but it all started to unravel at exceptional speed in the last 20 (or so) pages. The seeds were sown from the beginning about where Shiloh had gone and what he has done, but when Sarah finds this out all the other issues that crop up seem to overshadow the missing person case. It seems as though the author had a lot of ideas but just dumped them on the unsuspecting readers at the conclusion of the main story.<br /><br />I also felt that I had picked up the story half way through - I actually had to look up whether this was a second book in a series. Sadly I hadn't. This was the first book (of two) in a series but seemed like a lot of the background could have been best served in a prequel. </span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer153416524">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6372071619962467803">Because I live in Minnesota, I know that many of Ms. Comptons descriptions of Minnesota are fiction. For example, there is no Amtrak station in Blue Earth, girls basketball season doesn't start until November so there was no way that Gens sister Deborah was coaching a basketball game since this book took place in October. However, despite those inaccuracies, I still liked this book. It's fiction and since it's fiction anything can happen. However, one think that did bother me was that there real</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6372071619962467803">Because I live in Minnesota, I know that many of Ms. Comptons descriptions of Minnesota are fiction. For example, there is no Amtrak station in Blue Earth, girls basketball season doesn't start until November so there was no way that Gens sister Deborah was coaching a basketball game since this book took place in October. However, despite those inaccuracies, I still liked this book. It's fiction and since it's fiction anything can happen. However, one think that did bother me was that there really was no way Sarah would have been able to investigate her own husband disappearance. I'll read the next book in the series.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer308585105">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12749459067406782156">It was an interesting story, but it wasn't well-written. I'm used to reading the masters, like Koontz, Patterson, Crais - the ones who can weave the details of a story together so seamlessly, that if one were to remove even one detail, the entire story would fall apart. In the 37th Hour, there were great moments, but the moments didn't flow together. There were entire events and even characters that could have been removed, with no effect to the story. It seemed disjointed and at the end, I wond</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12749459067406782156">It was an interesting story, but it wasn't well-written. I'm used to reading the masters, like Koontz, Patterson, Crais - the ones who can weave the details of a story together so seamlessly, that if one were to remove even one detail, the entire story would fall apart. In the 37th Hour, there were great moments, but the moments didn't flow together. There were entire events and even characters that could have been removed, with no effect to the story. It seemed disjointed and at the end, I wondered why some of the things were even in there. The ending was disappointing and left even more loose ends.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2161672842597605644">I was pleased to find this debut novel and her sophomore title featuring the same main character, Sarah Pribek, on a recent library visit. The story was good and the characters interesting to get to know.<br /><br />What was especially a treat was Compton's stellar writing; she has a beautiful knack with the language that makes reading her books a pleasure. Also enjoyable is Compton's creation of Pribek, who is not a knight-in-shining-armor protagonist. Pribek has flaws and makes mistakes and has some serious personal baggages, but through it all, she is trying to do what is right.<br /><br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8mxIriZUOswSUm5zEXtxZd+Qn+qUO4eWgIlY0k/Uth+XuHd91IYuNp6KGshvGpfXlmdc893mwDzqgF1Ag0FAWg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('172I6VG7hKpYZBPhf0mfUPBs1EX7+cwaRuc0+QHZ+f2yabc6o2mQUNS8Z1oBKHniuZsXXLIki7As7jFrzUwPuA==')})
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/391769.Jodi_Compton">About Jodi Compton</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/391769.Jodi_Compton"><img alt="391769" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1303335974p2/391769.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer2515669382832289882">Jodi Compton, like Hailey Cain, is "Californian in a way a lot of people are Californian; I was born someplace else." Jodi has lived in California since the age of one, except for a brief stint in Minneapolis. In addition to the two Hailey Cain novels, Jodi is the author of two novels about Minneapolis detective Sarah Pribek, The 37th Hour and Sympathy Between Humans. She currently lives outside S</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2515669382832289882">Jodi Compton, like Hailey Cain, is "Californian in a way a lot of people are Californian; I was born someplace else." Jodi has lived in California since the age of one, except for a brief stint in Minneapolis. In addition to the two Hailey Cain novels, Jodi is the author of two novels about Minneapolis detective Sarah Pribek, The 37th Hour and Sympathy Between Humans. She currently lives outside San Luis Obispo with her Lab mix, Lady Bird.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2515669382832289882">...more</a>

Now Compton delivers a new novel featuring Detective&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText5703739611816747980\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;Jodi Compton’s debut, The 37th Hour, was hailed as “compelling” (San Francisco Chronicle), “intelligent” (New York Times Book Review), and “the debut of a world-class mystery writer” (Denver Post). Now Compton delivers a new novel featuring Detective Sarah Pribek, one of the most singular and complex characters in suspense fiction today.On the streets of Minneapolis, Sarah has worked everything from vice to missing persons. But six months after the death of a small-town criminal in rural Minnesota, Sarah is still protecting the identity of a killer. And now a zealous D.A.’s investigator has come to town, determined to make an arrest. With her ex-partner half a world away and her husband in prison, only Sarah remains to face the consequences of last fall. Surrounded by colleagues who know her to be the suspect in a murder, Sarah keeps her demons at bay by involving herself in the troubles of strangers. Seventeen-year-old Aidan Hennessy was banished from his family by his father. Now Aidan’s twin sister is desperately searching for the brother she hasn’t seen in years. Although the case is out of Sarah’s jurisdiction, she sees a reflection of herself in the troubled, damaged family, and agrees to investigate.As she probes into their tangled history, Sarah begins to realize that the mystery of the Hennessys runs deeper than it appears. Then Sarah’s lieutenant gives her a simpler assignment: Track down a doctor rumored to be practicing medicine without a license in a housing project. But in Cicero Ruiz, Sarah finds a tough, wounded survivor whose moral code challenges her own ideas about justice…and whose hard-won life would be destroyed by an arrest. Now juggling two very different cases, both requiring a delicate balancing act between professional honor and personal feelings, Sarah soon has even more at stake. Caught up in a cat-and-mouse game with the investigator who wants to end her career, crossing one ethical line after another, Sarah increasingly fears that a misstep on her part will end not only in her disgrace, but in the death of one of those she has promised herself to protect.With its fascinating heroine and its brilliantly interwoven mysteries, Sympathy Between Humans is storytelling at its finest from one of the most original and daring writers in suspense fiction today.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"5703739611816747980\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent($(this));; return
